Back to Agenda                                            AGENDA ITEM X-1
                                                                                         DRAFT
                              Finance Committee Meeting Minutes
                                    San Juan Water District
                                       December 8, 2025
                                          2:00 p.m.

    Committee Members:          Mike McRae, Director (Chair)
                                Manuel Zamorano, Director (Member)

    District Staff:             Adam Larsen, General Manager
                                Donna Silva, Director of Finance & Human Resources
                                Tony Barela, Director of Operations
                                Devon Barrett, Customer Service Manager
                                Teri Grant, Board Secretary/Administrative Assistant

    Members of the Public: User 01
                           Jennifer Farr, DavisFarr, Certified Public Accountants
                           Pam Tobin, SJWD Board Director
                           Meera Deshmane, SJWD Retail Customer


    1.   Presentation of Independent Audit Results by DavisFarr, Certified Public
         Accountants - Fiscal Year Ending June 30, 2025 (W & R)
         Ms. Silva introduced Jennifer Farr from DavisFarr, Certified Public Accountants, and
         explained that they conducted the independent audit of the District’s financials for fiscal
         year ending June 30, 2025. Ms. Farr informed the Committee that they started the audit
         procedures in April 2025 and moved onto the final audit in October 2025 after the
         District’s financial books were closed.

         Ms. Farr reported that they completed their work and issued an unmodified audit
         opinion on the financial statements. She explained that an unmodified audit opinion
         means that the financial statements are fairly stated in all material respects, which is
         the highest level of audit opinion that can be received.

         Ms. Farr informed the Committee that they found the books to be in excellent condition
         and District staff were prepared for the audit and responsive to their inquiries. There
         were no audit adjustments, and no material weaknesses or significant deficiencies in
         internal controls. She commended staff for their high level of competency.

         The Committee commended the Finance Staff and the auditing firm for their good work.

         In response to Director McRae’s question about new tools or different ways of doing
         business she would recommend for staff to do their job better, Ms. Farr informed the
         Committee that the auditors keep a housekeeping list for their clients as they perform
         the audit and usually there are a number of items that they suggest to clients; however,
         she stated that the District only had one item that they have on the list. She explained,
         that after the audit starts, the finance team will sometimes make adjustments to the
         numbers to make last minute adjustments prior to finalizing the audit, which is a minor
                                                                Finance Committee Meeting Minutes
                                                                                December 8, 2025
                                                                                          Page 2

     thing and she believes that it is a timing issue. Ms. Farr suggested that something to
     strive for is for the District to prepare their own financial statements in house. Ms. Silva
     agreed that it is a timing issue regarding the last minute entries as they are transfers
     which cannot be completed until everything else is completed. Ms. Silva informed the
     Committee that drafting the financial statements in-house is a staffing and workload
     issue.

     In response to Director McRae’s question, Ms. Silva informed the Committee that this
     is the 3rd year of a 4-year contract with DavisFarr, and the District will go out to bid for
     the contract. In response to Director McRae’s question, Ms. Farr explained that their
     firm does not look at the District’s incoming revenue vs. cost of debt service vs. project
     cost in order to judge the overall financial health of District.

     In response to Director Zamorano’s question, Ms. Silva explained that part of the
     reason there were no journal entries or adjustments from the auditors is because the
     finance department runs through a lot of analysis as part of the closing process to make
     sure that the books are clean.

     In response to Director McRae’s question, Ms. Silva confirmed that the property tax
     assessed value covers the total wholesale service area boundary.

     The Committee discussed having Ms. Farr present at the December Board meeting.
     Ms. Silva explained that the accounting firm usually presents to the Committee and
     then the item is placed on the Consent Calendar to receive and file.

     In response to Ms. Meera Deshmane’s question, Ms. Silva explained that the auditors
     do not look at the water rate calculations and do not review the rate study reports.

2.   Review General Manager Reimbursements (W & R)
     The Committee reviewed the credit card charges of the General Manager and found
     them to be in order. There were no reimbursement requests from the General Manager.

3.   Review Check Register from November 2025 (W & R)
     The Committee reviewed the November 2025 check register and found it to be in order.

4.   Review of Legal Bills (W & R)
     The Committee reviewed the legal bills and found them to be in order. Ms. Silva
     informed the Committee that she added the Prop. 218 legal counsel invoice from
     August.

5.   Retail Rate Structure Analysis (R)
     Director McRae reviewed his draft outline, which will be attached to the meeting
     minutes, and will make a PowerPoint presentation for the January 14th workshop.
     Director McRae recommends that the District continues pursuing the Board motion for
     the Finance Committee to bring a roadmap to the full Board for approval, with said
     roadmap to address those items identified throughout the discussion of this subject. He
     clarified that the analysis would include items such as looking into a gravity zone
     discount, how the fixed portion of the rate should be allocated, who pays for the capital
                                                               Finance Committee Meeting Minutes
                                                                               December 8, 2025
                                                                                         Page 3

     improvement projects, how property taxes are allocated (if not during this analysis, then
     at some point later), having different variable rates, and looking at tiered rates. Ms.
     Silva responded that she will include property tax information in her January 14th
     presentation. Director McRae confirmed that the roadmap is essentially the scope of
     work that a consultant would address.

     The Committee discussed the outline, gravity zone vs. pump zone water service and
     Prop. 218 issues. Director Zamorano pointed out that utilities were formed to spread
     the cost so that the benefit can reach everybody.

     Ms. Deshmane reflected on her previous challenges to the District on water rates and
     stated that a discount to the gravity zone is not really a discount since they are already
     paying more for services not being received. In response to her comment on Prop. 218,
     Director Zamorano explained that when he first read the language in Prop. 218 he
     agreed with her and Director McRae; however, there has been so much litigation
     regarding Prop. 218 and the scope of its impact is now much greater. In addition, he
     stated that the District is in compliance with the law as made perfectly clear by the Prop.
     218 expert, and the District’s rates are reasonable, and as a utility everybody benefits.
     Ms. Deshmane disagreed with Director Zamorano’s statement and asked that the
     District analyze the information before making a decision and proceed with their
     commitment to perform a retail rate study.

6.   Other Finance Matters (W & R)
     There were no other matters discussed.

7.   Public Comment
     There were no public comments.

The meeting was adjourned at 3:12 p.m.
                                          DRAFT: Work In Progress……
                                             (Convert below to a PowerPoint….)


                              Why Perform A Rate Structure Analysis?
BACKGROUND:
Detailed Customer Complaint….methodical….supported by data……convincing.
        * Volumetric cost of water.
        * Same Fixed Cost (regardless of actual cost of delivery)
        * Everyone pays for CIP projects, (regardless of who benefits).
Board Action…. (add text of motion..)

The Reason For This Public Outreach Meeting:
* To obtain feedback from Board Members, Staff, and the customer / owner.
* This feedback to be considered in developing the “Rate Analysis Roadmap”.
* This roadmap would basically be the high-level scope of work for a future rate-analysis consultant.

PERSPECTIVE:
(1) The customer / owners are the reason for the existence of the water district. As such, the water district is NOT and “end
in itself”……does not exist for it’s own benefit. Instead, it exists for the sole benefit of the customer owners. As such:
          * The district needs to put the customers interests before its own.
          * The district needs to maintain good financial health…..not for it’s own selfish interests, but for the benefit of the
owner/ customers.
          * NOTE: The district should never use the argument of “financial health” as an excuse to financially exploit the
customer / owners.
          • Like the concept of “Blindfolded Lady Justice”, the district should be impartial to the owner customers, and not
              favor one customer (or group of customers) over another.

(2) All good laws have a moral / ethical foundation….. To discourage lying, cheating, stealing, physically harming
someone….etc. (show 218 regulations slide…..make note of important textual items…..”one customer should not be forced
to pay towards another customers water bill”….

THE FUTURE ANALYSIS:
What an analysis would be……
   • Having a consultant analyze our rate structure with respect to cost of water delivery to different customer groups.
          o To analyze the customer/ owner challenge to the rate structure.
          o If the challenge is valid, then the goal being a more just (moral / ethical) application of the rate structure,
               that is in closer alignment with the 218 language.
          o The scope of this work would be defined in the pending “rate analysis roadmap”.
          o Depending on findings, the Board may be presented with one or more options to improve the retail customer
               rate structure.
   • Keeping the same overall rate revenue.
   • Keeping the same approved budget and approved project list.

What an analysis “would not” be….
  • Would not be a reduction in revenue.
  • Would not be a reduction in the budget or project list.
Examples of other water districts:
      • Riverside,
      • East Bay Municipal Utility District,
      • Indian Wells,
      • Casitas
      • Santa Margarita

           RECOMMENDATION: Continue pursuing the board motion for the Finance Committee to bring a roadmap to the
           full Board for approval. Said roadmap to address those items identified throughout the discussion of this subject.
